et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays cutting it until it is large, then take care if it is hard, of a dark color, of little feeling:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron for it is a cancerous abscess, for when it is cut sometimes, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then bleed the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and astringent things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the birthmark is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a break occurs in one of these cartilaginous structures, it heals poorly, except in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary when this happens to someone, to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips with a suture, then treat it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then you must scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then bring the two lips together with a suture, and tighten it, and sprinkle on powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put over the powders a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of suturing is that you bring together the separated parts:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the abdomen;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have explained to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In many men, hard abscesses appear inside the lips, resembling vetch grains, both smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn the lips, and cut into each lump, and grasp it with pincers and cut it on each side;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then fill the place after the incision with crushed vitriol, until the bleeding is stopped;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash it with vinegar, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times, extra flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so you must hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood flow;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the area crushed vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if this flesh returns after the incision, and it often does, then cut it a second time and cauterize it:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	thus it will not return after cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, so much so that the decay reaches the gums, and the teeth are foul-smelling;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	so you must have the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth where the scabs appear, until nothing remains there;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and do the same with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, until they are cleaned;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if what is there is removed on the first scraping, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then begin scraping again the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything away;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth require various shapes of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers with which one scrapes outside the teeth have other shapes than those with which one scrapes between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is advisable, when you treat a toothache, that you delay extracting it as long as you can, because one should not do this;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very important substance unless one has no other option than to extract it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is compelled to have it extracted, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have the good tooth extracted;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not go away because of this, until the bad one is extracted, for we have already seen this done to these healers;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are quite certain of the aching tooth, you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then loosen it with your fingers or with fine tongs at the first push and push, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the tongs;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then pull the tooth straight out without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it gently on each side, and move it as you did before. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is decayed and damaged, you must fill it with cloth, where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and grip it carefully with the tongs so that it doesn't break when pulled;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it, leaving a piece behind, which would cause the patient even greater pain than before due to the harmful nature of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be careful not to do as ignorant healers do, who through their haste and recklessness sometimes damage the gums and don’t achieve what we have described;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes, because of this, they cause serious illness due to the roots that remain, or because of the gum tissue they damage, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or vinegar and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with ground vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, which are used to move the teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so they don't bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick parts so they don't bend when pulling, and be made of good Indian steel, and be toothed for a firm grip.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after pulling, you must put on the spot cotton moistened with butter for one or two days, until the area is softened, then apply the forceps that are called "algefri", whose head resembles a heron's beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and inside they are made like a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these forceps, then you must expose the flesh all around the root, and apply the instrument called "althali", that is to say, a levator, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out because of this, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, then help yourself with all the instruments, the forms of which follow here below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are earlier in the section on teeth, and this instrument that resembles large forceps/pincers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted/mentioned;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise and subtle master finds for himself his instrument, according to what his works and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of bones, and if one does not break the cartilage or the other bones, where it is decayed, then he searches for the instruments that are suitable there, as I have told you, and makes use of the procedures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and gripping well to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then scrape it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in young women, then you must know if the tooth has grown behind the (other) tooth, and is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or polished:
adonques lou raie;	then scrape it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if there is space beside the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be made of Indian steel, sharp at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days, due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with such a file as is shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is like the file with which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and file the tooth little by little over many days, lightly, so that it does not move until it falls out;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then smooth it at the end with some kind of scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and injures the tongue, it should be filed down until it is even, so that it does not injure the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth become loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth become loose, either by being struck or by falling, and the patient cannot chew what they eat without them falling out, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and it is of no use;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then they must be bound with a gold wire, because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and the wire should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the wire and put it doubled between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you come carefully to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then repeat the wrapping up to the part where you began, and tighten it carefully and skillfully with your hand, so that it does not move;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and the ligature should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers, and bring them together, and fold them back between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it tightened as much as possible, and if it comes loose, or the wire breaks, tighten it with another wire;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	it will remain and serve thus for its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the illustration of the straightening of the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth from cow bone, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this frenulum that comes from under the tongue is natural, that one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the procedure is such that you open the patient's mouth, and have his head on your lap, and lift his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nervous frenulum widely, so that the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, and it is from the healing of a wound, then insert the hook and cut that ligament widely;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the cut is not too deep, because of the artery that is underneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have finished, wash the area with rose water and vinegar, or with cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and the patient should hold it there each night, so that the area cannot close up.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, apply crushed vitriol to the area;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding overcomes you, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with other remedies until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it with a dark or black or hard color, so that the patient cannot feel it, do not touch it at all, because it is a canker;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is tending towards white, and there is moisture, then apply a hook, and split it with a fine spatula, and free it on one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the bleeding overcomes you in your work, apply ground vitriol until it is stopped, then return to your work until you draw out all the fire (or core); 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean the place with vinegar and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes lumps come inside the throat which are called "godath," and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the section (or chapter), and they are not healed, then take note:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess with little feeling and a dark color, do not touch it with iron (a surgical instrument).
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the base is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the risk of bleeding;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will rupture on its own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is a round white color, and the base is thin, have the instrument ready to cut, but first check if the abscess is calm and appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with their head in your lap, have them open their mouth, and have the assistant take their head between their hands and press the tongue down with the instrument, the shape of which is shown here;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be made of silver or thin brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue down with this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the hook and insert it into the tonsil, and pull it out above as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull some of the tissue with it, then cut it with the instrument, the shape of which is shown here, that looks like scissors;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and the tips are curved, and one towards the other, and are very sharp, and made of Indian steel or hardened steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, cut it with forceps/pincers, of which the shape is shown here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be sharp on one side, and not on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same way, and after the incision, have the patient gargle with hot water, and water and vinegar, and if bleeding occurs, have the patient gargle with water, in which pomegranate rinds have been boiled, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat him until he is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them in the same way as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say, an abscess of little sensation;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained that way for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that two tubes had been placed through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore acted quickly and inserted a hook into one of them, then pulled it out, and drew out a large amount of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I did the same in the other nostril, and I worked her mouth and pressed her tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	afterwards I inserted the hook into these abscesses, and cut a part of them, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the woman's throat passage was opened, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess kept growing back, filling the space that I had emptied, until it was very large again;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I tricked it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it stopped growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts, and I don't know what God did with her after me. 
de l’uve	of the uvula
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When a rheum descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is large and round underneath, it is called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have described in the section, and the treatment is not effective, and you see that the hot abscess is subsided, and it is thin, then you must cut it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is round and compact and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or dark-colored or black, then you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have described, by its whiteness and its length, that you have the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned earlier;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the hook into the uvula, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned for the incision of the tonsils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have described for the incision of the tonsils, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you must use a trick for cauterization without him fearing.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is with sharp water. (or: And the way of the cautery is with sharp water.)
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And the patient should place his head on your lap, and then you press the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and moisten it with hot vinegar, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and fill the hollow of this instrument, of which here is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it has a bowl at the end where the medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the uvula;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be lying on his side, so that the saliva and mucus run out of his mouth with the medicine inside, so that it doesn't go down the throat and harm him; 
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it on the uvula, for about half an hour, until you see it numbed and the burning sensation of the medicine has subsided;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with the cotton in the mouth above, so that the cotton rests on the uvula;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry, and it will fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to repeat the cauterization with the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cauterization wipe around the uvula, with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and it should be rinsed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, or than cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and southernwood and similar herbs, and put them all together or some of them in a pot, and add vinegar, and boil it;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be a hollow instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be made of silver or brass, and one end should be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the uvula through the tube, until the uvula is deadened;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	afterwards repeat it often, until the uvula dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of the hot abscess, because several things can happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not perform this cauterization until the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, then take a tube and place inside the end an eggshell, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the eggshell does not allow the vapor to irritate the mouth, and this is a good treatment together with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times a bone or fishbone, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	therefore you must pull out what you can see, and depress the tongue with the instrument towards the light, so that you can see the thing move; 
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps the stuck object will come out through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a lettuce root, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it reaches the spot, it will swell, and then you will pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it doesn't come out with what we've said, then take a lead instrument of this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the tip raised upwards;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that coughing does not occur, nor push the bone inwards;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it's better that the patient inserts the instrument, because he knows better where the thing is lodged;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	then he pushes it down, or pulls it out with the instrument evenly, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the leech in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the leech is treated, as I have said in the division, by the application of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when that is not effective, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you have pressed down their tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, then pull it out whole with a small hook, or with fine forceps suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, then take a hollow cane, and put it into the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the hollow of the cane, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient abstain from water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a glass full of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with his hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the leech feels the water, it will fall off.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it doesn't fall off as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I described in the fumigation of the uvula;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this several times, because it will fall off without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot containing live coals, and the pot should be covered with a lid pierced in the middle, and in this hole should be the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then throw your fumigant in it, and the patient puts the end of the tube in his mouth and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the leech;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the leech will fall off immediately, and if it does not fall off, repeat the fumigation several times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty and sharp things, and do not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary that it comes out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one extracts the leech, if one can see it, is similar to curved tongs made to enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it has a resemblance to the beak of a snipe, and has a roughness from a file, so that what it grips, it cannot release;
et vez ci la forme:	and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	There are many kinds of abscesses, as will be recalled later in this book, one after another, and they differ in perforation and in incision;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways, one of which is in its appearance itself, and in that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is because of the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For an abscess of the head is different from one of the buttocks, and an abscess of a fleshy place is different from one that occurs in the joints, and each has its own treatment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And there are abscesses that one should not pierce, until the pus is ripe according to its maturation;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are some that must be pierced when they are raw, and do not ripen according to their maturation, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess develops near the joints, and it is left until it rots around it, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is ripened, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or it is near the anus, so it is pierced before it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and you should not pierce a raw abscess without complete digestion, except for the one that is near the anus, so that it does not rot deeply inside, and become elongated within, and a fistula develops there;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the time for the piercing of the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the throbbing and the sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you should make the perforation in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears soft;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the perforation should be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all similar places where there is no bending.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, along the length of that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the poison will be elongated, and it is full of much filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps the edges and the depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And there are some abscesses that are pierced along the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must manage, with small abscesses, small openings;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and with large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and there are some abscesses where it is necessary to shave the core and cut;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become yellow like a cloth, and is dead, one must do as one does with buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and there are some that are split into three angles, and there are some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the groin; 
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and there are some where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, you must pierce completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a lot of pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that time, but draw out a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then plug the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more again;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times, little by little, until all the pus comes out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or a decrepit old man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes leaps out with the exit of the pus, so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound and see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a full incision, then administer tents of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must put a tent in each one so that they come against each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have lifted it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or lint from linen cloths without moisture, and tie it up until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, then administer cold water and vinegar, and wet a cloth, and place it on the bleeding area several times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding continues, administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in many places in this book, and if it is in winter, and the area where the abscess is located is very sensitive, then you must put on tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, you should apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess and drain it and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this should be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of scrofula
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the head small abscesses arise, and they are like knots which are in webs, like the wattles of a hen, and there are many that are similar.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some of them fat and some in which there is moisture like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and there are some which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no danger unless an artery interferes.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cutting is that you test with an instrument which is called a "probe," the form of which comes hereafter, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then split it lengthwise from above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is emptied, then flay without leaving anything of the skin that contains this moisture, for it always returns if anything is left;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and this will corrode what remains of the dead tissue.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then replace the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that none of the dead tissue remains;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with a suitable ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds a core of fatty substance, cut it along its length, in this way;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and insert your hooks, and peel it away on all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out the covering where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery gives you trouble, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with the abscess if it is stony, both in cutting and treating it as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on a stony abscess, and a moist one, is easier, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses are on the head where there is no moisture, as there was one abscess I cut from the head of an old woman; 
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess like a rough, coarse, and white stone, and it could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck it, one would have made a wound in it like in a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses occurring on the head, except those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent place, to allow the pus to drain;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and they are numerous and intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrophulous swelling is properly within its own membrane, like the kernel and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the variations of these scrofulous swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not respond to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In the one that you see to be of good disposition to the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and movable on all sides and is not near the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the throat, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	you should cut it from above, and peel it on each side, and spread the two lips of the core with hooks, if you need them, as we have said for abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and pull it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and the spatula should not be sharp or pointed, so that the hand does not slip, and does not go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and this prevents you from working, put ground vitriol into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and compress the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then search with your index finger if any small scrofulas remain, then cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you should not cut this scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, you must bring the two edges of the wound together, and sew them immediately, then make sure there is no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must take care to cut the root of it, and draw out fire, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that contain excess fluid, pierce them where they appear ripe;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it like the one mentioned before, downwards, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it dissolves what remains of the corrupted matter;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then treat it with ointment generating flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke and discussed the incision of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have quinsy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and that no help be given by this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are [affected] in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the trachea of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three or four rings, a small transverse incision, between the two rings or by the amount of the incision of the uvula, but not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and this place is suitable for the incision of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are far from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the practitioner is fearful, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat with the hook, then cut the flesh until he reaches the trachea;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the uvula, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the expulsion of phlegm from the trachea which jumps out through the place that is opened, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the time has passed during which strangulation is feared, bring together the two lips of the wound of the flesh, and sew it alone without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged near death, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then one cuts the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the danger of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they instructed to sew the wound and treat it, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young woman take a knife, and stick it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the lung;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood which had come out, and knew well that she had not cut a vein or any vessel but the throat, and the wind was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the young woman except that her voice was hoarse, and later returned to normal;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no need for fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat/windpipe
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess the color of soot, and is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is of two kinds:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	in the natural one there is no trick/deceit.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is of two kinds, one of which resembles a fatty knot, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from a knotted artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not appropriate to operate with fire except in the one that is small, and test and examine it with a probe:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a fatty knot, and it is not attached to any vein, cut it as one cuts knots, and pull it out with its entire covering, if it has any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and carefully examine everything, and treat it as appropriate, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the knots/tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of lumps, of which I will describe all the appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must explain all the differences between a lump and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an ulcer involves heat and persistent fever, until the boiling is over, and the suppuration is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a lump there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a syfac, which is its own sac and is the same color as the body, and begins like a bean and grows large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and there are two types, either fatty or moist, and of many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the lump, that you first examine and probe it with the instrument called "probe", according to the form which will come in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way to examine the abscesses of the lumps is that you take the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, provided that it is according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the probe, and pay attention to what comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If a thin, flowing moisture comes out, note what color it is, and smell it as I have said of other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if no moisture comes out after the probe, know that it is fatty, then cut it crosswise, and take it with forceps, and peel it gently from each side and watch the skin in which it lies so that you pull it out whole with the lump;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the lump will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains, and the blood troubles you, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and constrict the wound, and apply soothing things for a hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the lump is large, then sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the pulsating vein or other [vessel] hinders you, then hurry and fill the area with crushed vitriol, and leave it there for two or three days, until the wound rots, and the boiling of the blood subsides;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cutting what remains of the lump.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of the intermediary instruments, and they are of three types:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three square ones which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three types of them:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to probe the abscesses of a fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles with which one sews wounds, and they are of yellow brass, or of iron, or of silver, and the yellow ones are worth more, and those made of black lead are better tested for probing the curvature of a fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three types:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the hooks are of many resemblances, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are hooks that have two curves of three types also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are hooks that have three curves, and they are also of three types;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are hooks that have two curves, and hooks of only one curve, and they are of three types;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these with which one cuts are sharp, and of such there are some that do not cut except on one side, with which one flays the sinews, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these inserters are the lancets placed in handles, so that the patients do not perceive them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three types:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and they are used only in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and the groin, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling pistachio shells, according to this shape, with which blood is stanched:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed at the site that heals by severing veins, and arteries, and sometimes they are round according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much so that they resemble women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them, must cauterize them according to this shape from this line b. down to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape away the fat, and fill the wound with medicine generating flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops down and is softened by its size as happens with women, then split it into two parts from above, with two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of which one is connected to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b. down to line g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
